<pre tabindex="0" style="color:#f8f8f2;background-color:#272822;-moz-tab-size:4;-o-tab-size:4;tab-size:4;"><code class="language-text" data-lang="text"><span style="display:flex;"><span>He existed before anything other than himself    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>came into being.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Father is a single one, like a number, for   |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>himself.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Yet he is not like a solitary individual.        |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>But the single one, who alone is the Father,     |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is said of him that he is a father in the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>proper sense, since he is inimitable and         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>immutable.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Because of this, he is single in the proper      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>sense, and is a god, because no one is a god     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for him nor is anyone a father to him.           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For he is unbegotten, and there is no other      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who begot him, nor another who created him.      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For whoever is someone&#39;s father or his           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>creator, he, too, has a father and creator.      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is certainly possible for him to be father    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and creator of the one who came into being       |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is not a father in the proper sense, nor a       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>god, because he has someone who begot him and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who created him.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is, then, only the Father and God in the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>proper sense that no one else begot.             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>As for the Totalities, he is the one who begot   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>them and created them.                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He is without beginning and without end.         |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>To say anything of this sort is ignorant.        |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>since he knows himself as he is.                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>What is worthy of his admiration and glory and   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>honor and praise, he produces because of the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>boundlessness of his greatness, and the          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>unsearchability of his wisdom, and the           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>immeasurability of his power, and his            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>untasteable sweetness.                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He is the one who projects himself thus, as      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>generation, having glory and honor marvelous     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and lovely; the one who glorifies himself, who   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>marvels, &lt;who&gt; honors, who also loves; the one   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who has a Son, who subsists in him, who is       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>silent concerning him, who is the ineffable      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one in the ineffable one, the invisible one,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the incomprehensible one, the inconceivable      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one in the inconceivable one.                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Thus, he exists in him forever.                  |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Father, in the way we mentioned earlier,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in an unbegotten way, is the one in whom he      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>knows himself, who begot him having a thought,   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which is the thought of him, that is, the        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>perception of him, which is the [...] of his     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>constitution forever.                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>That is, however, in the proper sense, the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>silence and the wisdom and the grace, if it is   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>designated properly in this way.                 |</span></span></code></pre></td></tr></table>
</div>
</div>

<pre tabindex="0" style="color:#f8f8f2;background-color:#272822;-moz-tab-size:4;-o-tab-size:4;tab-size:4;"><code class="language-text" data-lang="text"><span style="display:flex;"><span>Just as the Father exists in the proper sense,   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the one before whom there was no one else, and   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the one apart from whom there is no other        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>unbegotten one, so too the Son exists in the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>proper sense, the one before whom there was no   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>other, and after whom no other son exists.       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, he is a firstborn and an only Son,    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>&#34;firstborn&#34; because no one exists before him     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and &#34;only Son&#34; because no one is after him.      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Furthermore, he has his fruit, that which is     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>unknowable because of its surpassing             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>greatness.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Yet he wanted it to be known, because of the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>riches of his sweetness.                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>And he revealed the unexplainable power, and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>he combined with it the great abundance of his   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>generosity.                                      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Not only did the Son exist from the beginning,   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>but the Church, too, existed from the            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beginning.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Now, he who thinks that the discovery that the   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Son is an only son opposes the statement         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>(about the Church) because of the mysterious     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>quality of the matter, it is not so.             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For just as the Father is a unity, and has       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>revealed himself as Father for him alone, so     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>too the Son was found to be a brother to         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>himself alone, in virtue of the fact that he     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is unbegotten and without beginning.             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He wonders at himself, along with the Father,    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and he gives him(self) glory and honor and       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>love.                                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Furthermore, he too is the one whom he           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>conceives of as Son, in accordance with the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>dispositions: &#34;without beginning&#34; and &#34;without   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>end.&#34; Thus is the matter something which is      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>fixed.                                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Being innumerable and illimitable, his           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>offspring are indivisible.                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Those which exist have come forth from the Son   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and the Father like kisses, because of the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>multitude of some who kiss one another with a    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>good, insatiable thought, the kiss being a       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>unity, although it involves many kisses.         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>This is to say, it is the Church consisting of   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>many men that existed before the aeons, which    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is called, in the proper sense, &#34;the aeons of    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the aeons.&#34; This is the nature of the holy       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>imperishable spirits, upon which the Son         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>rests, since it is his essence, just as the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father rests upon the Son.                       |</span></span></code></pre></td></tr></table>

<td style="vertical-align:top;padding:0;margin:0;border:0;;width:100%">
<pre tabindex="0" style="color:#f8f8f2;background-color:#272822;-moz-tab-size:4;-o-tab-size:4;tab-size:4;"><code class="language-text" data-lang="text"><span style="display:flex;"><span>[...] the Church exists in the dispositions      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and properties in which the Father and the Son   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>exist, as I have said from the start.            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, it subsists in the procreations of    |  The Church continues to exist in procreations
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>innumerable aeons.                               |  of aeons.
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Also in an uncountable way they too beget, by    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the properties and the dispositions in which     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>it (the Church) exists.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For these comprise its association which they    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>form toward one another and toward those who     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>have come forth from them toward the Son, for    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>whose glory they exist.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, it is not possible for mind to        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>conceive of him - He was the perfection of       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>that place - nor can speech express them, for    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they are ineffable and unnameable and            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>inconceivable.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They alone have the ability to name themselves   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and to conceive of themselves.                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For they have not been rooted in these places.   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Those of that place are ineffable, (and)         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>innumerable in the system which is both the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>manner and the size, the joy, the gladness of    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the unbegotten, nameless, unnameable,            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>inconceivable, invisible, incomprehensible       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one.                                             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is the fullness of paternity, so that his     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>abundance is a begetting [...] of the aeons.     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They were forever in thought, for the Father     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>was like a thought and a place for them.         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>When their generations had been established,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the one who is completely in control wished to   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>lay hold of and to bring forth that which was    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>deficient in the [...] and he brought forth      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>those [...] him.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>But since he is as he is, he is a spring,        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which is not diminished by the water which       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>abundantly flows from it.                        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>While they were in the Father&#39;s thought, that    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is, in the hidden depth, the depth knew them,    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>but they were unable to know the depth in        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which they were; nor was it possible for them    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to know themselves, nor for them to know         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>anything else.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>That is, they were with the Father; they did     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>not exist for themselves.                        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Rather, they only had existence in the manner    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of a seed, so that it has been discovered that   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they existed like a fetus.                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Like the word he begot them, subsisting          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>spermatically, and the ones whom he was to       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beget had not yet come into being from him.      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The one who first thought of them, the Father,   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>- not only so that they might exist for him,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>but also that they might exist for themselves    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>as well, that they might then exist in his       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>thought as mental substance and that they        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>might exist for themselves too, - sowed a        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>thought like a spermatic seed.                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Now, in order that they might know what exists   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for them, he graciously granted the initial      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>form, while in order that they might recognize   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who is the Father who exists for them, he gave   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>them the name &#34;Father&#34; by means of a voice       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>proclaiming to them that what exists, exists     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>through that name, which they have by virtue     |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the exaltation, which has escaped their          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>notice, is in the name.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The infant, while in the form of a fetus has     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>enough for itself, before ever seeing the one    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who sowed it.                                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, they had the sole task of searching   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for him, realizing that he exists, ever          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wishing to find out what exists.                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Since, however, the perfect Father is good,      |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they would exist (only) in his thought, but      |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>place: when they are born, they are in the       |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Father brought forth everything, like a      |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>There is no need for voice and spirit, mind      |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For this is their procreative power, like        |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they were seeking after him.                     |

</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Innumerable and indivisible are the begettings   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of his words, and his commands and his           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities.                                      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He knows them, which things he himself is,       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>since they are in the single name, and are all   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>speaking in it.                                  |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>And he brings (them) forth, in order that it     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>might be discovered that they exist according    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to their individual properties in a unified      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>way.                                             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>And he did not reveal the multitude to the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities at once nor did he reveal his         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>equality to those who had come forth from him.   |</span></span></code></pre></td></tr></table>
</div>
</div>

<td style="vertical-align:top;padding:0;margin:0;border:0;;width:100%">
<pre tabindex="0" style="color:#f8f8f2;background-color:#272822;-moz-tab-size:4;-o-tab-size:4;tab-size:4;"><code class="language-text" data-lang="text"><span style="display:flex;"><span>All those who came forth from him &lt;who&gt; are      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the aeons of the aeons, being emanations and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>offspring of &lt;his&gt; procreative nature, they      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>too, in their procreative nature, have &lt;given&gt;   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glory to the Father, as he was the cause of      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>their establishment.                             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>This is what we said previously, namely that     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>he creates the aeons as roots and springs and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>fathers, and that he is the one to whom they     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>give glory.                                      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They have begotten, for he has knowledge and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wisdom and the Totalities knew that it is from   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>knowledge and wisdom that they have come         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth.                                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They would have brought forth a seeming honor:   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>&#34;The Father is the one who is the Totalities,&#34;   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>if the aeons had risen up to give honor          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>individually.                                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, in the song of glorification and in   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the power of the unity of him from whom they     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>have come, they were drawn into a mingling and   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>a combination and a unity with one another.      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They offered glory worthy of the Father from     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the pleromatic congregation, which is a single   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>representation although many, because it was     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>brought forth as a glory for the single one      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and because they came forth toward the one who   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is himself the Totalities.                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Now, this was a praise [...] the one who         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>brought forth the Totalities, being a first-     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>fruit of the immortals and an eternal one,       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>because, having come forth from the living       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>aeons, being perfect and full because of the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one who is perfect and full, it left full and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>perfect those who have given glory in a          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>perfect way because of the fellowship.           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For, like the faultless Father, when he is       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glorified he also hears the glory which          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glorifies him, so as to make them manifest as    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>that which he is.                                |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The cause of the second honor which accrued to   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>them is that which was returned to them from     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the Father when they had known the grace by      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which they bore fruit with one another because   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of the Father.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>As a result, just as they &lt;were&gt; brought forth   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in glory for the Father, so too in order to      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>appear perfect, they appeared acting by giving   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glory.                                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They were fathers of the third glory according   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to the independence and the power which was      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>begotten with them, since each one of them       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>individually does not exist so as to give        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glory in a unitary way to him whom he loves.     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They are the first and the second and thus       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>both of them are perfect and full, for they      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>are manifestations of the Father who is          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>perfect and full, as well as of those who came   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth, who are perfect by the fact that they     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glorify the perfect one.                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The fruit of the third, however, consists of     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>honors of the will of each one of the aeons,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and each one of the properties.                  |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Father has power.                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It exists fully, perfect in the thought which    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is a product of agreement, since it is a         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>product of the individuality of the aeons.       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is this which he loves and over which he      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>has power, as it gives glory to the Father by    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>means of it.                                     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For this reason, they are minds of minds,        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which are found to be words of words, elders     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of elders, degrees of degrees, which are         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>exalted above one another.                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Each one of those who give glory has his place   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and his exaltation and his dwelling and his      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>rest, which consists of the glory which he       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>brings forth.                                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>All those who glorify the Father have their      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>begetting eternally, - they beget in the act     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of assisting one another - since the             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>emanations are limitless and immeasurable and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>since there is no envy on the part of the        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father toward those who came forth from him in   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>regard to their begetting something equal or     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>similar to him, since he is the one who exists   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in the Totalities, begetting and revealing       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>himself.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Whomever he wishes, he makes into a father, of   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>whom he in fact is Father, and a god, of whom    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>he in fact is God, and he makes them the         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities, whose entirety he is.                |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>In the proper sense all the names which are      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>great are kept there, these (names) which the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>angels share, who have come into being in the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>cosmos along with the archons, although they     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>do not have any resemblance to the eternal       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beings.                                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The entire system of the aeons has a love and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>a longing for the perfect, complete discovery    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of the Father and this is their unimpeded        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>agreement.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Though the Father reveals himself eternally,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>he did not wish that they should know him,       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>since he grants that he be conceived of in       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>such a way as to be sought for, while keeping    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to himself his unsearchable primordial being.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is he, the Father, who gave root impulses     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to the aeons, since they are places on the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>path which leads toward him, as toward a         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>school of behavior.                              |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He has extended to them faith in and prayer to   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him whom they do not see; and a firm hope in     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him of whom they do not conceive; and a          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>fruitful love, which looks toward that which     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>it does not see; and an acceptable               |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>understanding of the eternal mind; and a         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>blessing, which is riches and freedom; and a     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wisdom of the one who desires the glory of the   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father for &lt;his&gt; thought.                        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is by virtue of his will that the Father,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the one who is exalted, is known, that is, (by   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>virtue of) the spirit which breathes in the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities and it gives them an idea of          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>seeking after the unknown one, just as one is    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>drawn by a pleasant aroma to search for the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>thing from which the aroma arises, since the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>aroma of the Father surpasses these ordinary     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>ones.                                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For his sweetness leaves the aeons in            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>ineffable pleasure and it gives them their       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>idea of mingling with him who wants them to      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>know him in a united way and to assist one       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>another in the spirit which is sown within       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>them.                                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Though existing under a great weight, they are   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>renewed in an inexpressible way, since it is     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>impossible for them to be separated from that    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in which they are set in an uncomprehending      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>way, because they will not speak, being silent   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>about the Father&#39;s glory, about the one who      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>has power to speak, and yet they will take       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>form from him.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He revealed himself, though it is impossible     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to speak of him.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They have him, hidden in a thought, since from   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>this one [...].                                  |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They are silent about the way the Father is in   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>his form and his nature and his greatness,       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>while the aeons have become worthy of knowing    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>through his spirit that he is unnameable and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>incomprehensible.                                |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is through his spirit, which is the trace     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of the search for him, that he provides them     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the ability to conceive of him and to speak      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>about him.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Each one of the aeons is a name, &lt;that is&gt;,      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>each of the properties and powers of the         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father, since he exists in many names, which     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>are intermingled and harmonious with one         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>another.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is possible to speak of him because of the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wealth of speech, just as the Father is a        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>single name, because he is a unity, yet is       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>innumerable in his properties and names.         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The emanation of the Totalities, which exist     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>from the one who exists, did not occur           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>according to a separation from one another, as   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>something cast off from the one who begets       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>them.                                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Rather, their begetting is like a process of     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>extension, as the Father extends himself to      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>those whom he loves, so that those who have      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>come forth from him might become him as well.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Just as the present aeon, though a unity, is     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>divided by units of time and units of time are   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>divided into years and years are divided into    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>seasons and seasons into months, and months      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>into days, and days into hours, and hours into   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>moments, so too the aeon of the Truth, since     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>it is a unity and multiplicity, receives honor   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in the small and the great names according to    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the power of each to grasp it - by way of        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>analogy - like a spring which is what it is,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>yet flows into streams and lakes and canals      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and branches, or like a root spread out          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beneath trees and branches with its fruit, or    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>like a human body, which is partitioned in an    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>indivisible way into members of members,         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>primary members and secondary, great and         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>small.                                           |</span></span></code></pre></td></tr></table>
</div>
</div>

<td style="vertical-align:top;padding:0;margin:0;border:0;;width:100%">
<pre tabindex="0" style="color:#f8f8f2;background-color:#272822;-moz-tab-size:4;-o-tab-size:4;tab-size:4;"><code class="language-text" data-lang="text"><span style="display:flex;"><span>The aeons have brought themselves forth in       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>accord with the third fruit by the freedom of    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the will and by the wisdom with which he         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>favored them for their thought.                  |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They do not wish to give honor with that which   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is from an agreement, though it was produced     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for words of praise for each of the Pleromas.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Nor do they wish to give honor with the          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totality.                                        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Nor do they wish (to do so) with anyone else     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who was originally above the depth of that       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one, or (above) his place, except, however,      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for the one who exists in an exalted name and    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in the exalted place, and only if he receives    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>from the one who wished (to give honor), and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>takes it to him(self) for the one above him,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and (only if) he begets him(self), so to         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>speak, himself, and, through that one, begets    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him(self) along with that which he is, and       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>himself becomes renewed along with the one who   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>came upon him, by his brother, and sees him      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and entreats him about the matter, namely, he    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who wished to ascend to him.                     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>So that it might be in this way, the one who     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wished to give honor does not say anything to    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him about this, except only that there is a      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>limit to speech set in the Pleroma, so that      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they are silent about the incomprehensibility    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of the Father, but they speak about the one      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>who wishes to comprehend him.                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It came to one of the aeons that he should       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>attempt to grasp the incomprehensibility and     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>give glory to it and especially to the           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>ineffability of the Father.                      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Since he is a Logos of the unity, he is one,     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>though he is not from the agreement of the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities, nor from him who brought them        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth, namely, the one who brought forth the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totality, the Father.                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>This aeon was among those to whom was given      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wisdom, so that he could become pre-existent     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in each one&#39;s thought.                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>By that which he wills, will they be produced.   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, he received a wise nature in order    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to examine the hidden basis, since he is a       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>wise fruit; for, the free will which was         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>begotten with the Totalities was a cause for     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>this one, such as to make him do what he         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>desired, with no one to restrain him.            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The intent, then, of the Logos, who is this      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one, was good.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>When he had come forth, he gave glory to the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father, even if it led to something beyond       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>possibility, since he had wanted to bring        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth one who is perfect, from an agreement in   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which he had not been, and without having the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>command.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>This aeon was last to have &lt;been&gt; brought        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth by mutual assistance, and he was small     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>in magnitude.                                    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>And before he begot anything else for the        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glory of the will and in agreement with the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Totalities, he acted, magnanimously, from an     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>abundant love, and set out toward that which     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>surrounds the perfect glory, for it was not      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>without the will of the Father that the Logos    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>was produced, which is to say, not without it    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>will he go forth.                                |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>But he, the Father, had brought him forth for    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>those about whom he knew that it was fitting     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>that they should come into being.                |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Father and the Totalities drew away from     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him, so that the limit which the Father had      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>set might be established - for it is not from    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>grasping the incomprehensibility but by the      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>will of the Father, - and furthermore, (they     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>withdrew) so that the things which have come     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>to be might become an organization which would   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>come into being.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>If it were to come, it would not come into       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>being by the manifestation of the Pleroma.       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, it is not fitting to criticize the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>movement which is the Logos, but it is fitting   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>that we should say about the movement of the     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Logos that it is a cause of an organization      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which has been destined to come about.           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The Logos himself caused it to happen, being     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>complete and unitary, for the glory of the       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Father, whom he desired, and (he did so) being   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>content with it, but those whom he wished to     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>take hold of firmly he begot in shadows and      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>copies and likenesses.                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For, he was not able to bear the sight of the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>light, but he looked into the depth and he       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>doubted.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Out of this there was a division - he became     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>deeply troubled - and a turning away because     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of his self-doubt and division, forgetfulness    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and ignorance of himself and &lt;of that&gt; which     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>is.                                              |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>His self-exaltation and his expectation of       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>comprehending the incomprehensible became firm   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>for him and was in him.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>But the sicknesses followed him when he went     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beyond himself, having come into being from      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>self-doubt, namely from the fact that he did     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>not &lt;reach the attainment of&gt; the glories of     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the Father, the one whose exalted status is      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>among things unlimited.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>This one did not attain him, for he did not      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>receive him.                                     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The one whom he himself brought forth as a       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>unitary aeon rushed up to that which is his      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>and this kin of his in the Pleroma abandoned     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him who came to be in the defect along with      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>those who had come forth from him in an          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>imaginary way, since they are not his.           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>When he who produced himself as perfect          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>actually did bring himself forth, he became      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>weak like a female nature which has abandoned    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>its virile counterpart.                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>From that which was deficient in itself there    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>came those things which came into being from     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>his thought and his arrogance, but from that     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>which is perfect in him he left it and raised    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>himself up to those who are his.                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>He was in the Pleroma as a remembrance for him   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>so that he would be saved from his arrogance.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The one who ran on high and the one who drew     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>him to himself were not barren, but in           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>bringing forth a fruit in the Pleroma, they      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>upset those who were in the defect.              |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Like the Pleromas are the things which came      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>into being from the arrogant thought, which      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>are their (the Pleromas&#39;) likenesses, copies,    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>shadows, and phantasms, lacking reason and the   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>light, these which belong to the vain thought,   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>since they are not products of anything.         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, their end will be like their          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beginning: from that which did not exist (they   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>are) to return once again to that which will     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>not be.                                          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>It is they, however, by themselves who are       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>greater, more powerful, and more honored than    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the names which are given to them, which are     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>their shadows.                                   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>In the manner of a reflection are they           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beautiful.                                       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>For the face of the copy normally takes its      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beauty from that of which it is a copy.          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They thought of themselves that they are         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>beings existing by themselves and are without    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>a source, since they do not see anything else    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>existing before them.                            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, they lived in disobedience and acts   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>of rebellion, without having humbled             |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>themselves before the one because of whom they   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>came into being.                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They wanted to command one another, overcoming   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one another in their vain ambition, while the    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>glory which they possess contains a cause of     |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>the system which was to be.                      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They are likenesses of the things which are      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>exalted.                                         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They were brought to a lust for power in each    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>one of them, according to the greatness of the   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>name of which each is a shadow, each one         |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>imagining that it is superior to his fellows.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>The thought of these others was not barren,      |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>but just like &lt;those&gt; of which they are          |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>shadows, all that they thought about they have   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>as potential sons; those of whom they thought    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>they had as offspring.                           |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>Therefore, it happened that many offspring       |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>came forth from them, as fighters, as            |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>warriors, as troublemakers, as apostates.        |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>They are disobedient beings, lovers of power.    |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>                                                 |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>All the other beings of this sort were brought   |
</span></span><span style="display:flex;"><span>forth from these.                                |</span></span></code></pre></td></tr></table>
</div>
</div>
